## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator problem where acceleration (dv/dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The relationship encodes Newton's second law with nonlinear restoring forces, possible damping, and possible external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic spring + damping)
- Duffing with quintic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Driven damped harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (forced linear oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric + symmetric nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2)**(-0.5) * v (velocity-dependent friction approximation)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Full Duffing with damping and drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (canonical driven Duffing)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * abs(v) (aerodynamic drag)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x┬│, xŌüĄ) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium ŌĆö use odd polynomial in x
- Even-power terms in position (x┬▓) break oscillation symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation or injection (damping/driving)
- Product terms like x┬▓*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type oscillators
- Sinusoidal time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) indicates periodic external driving force
- Sinusoidal position dependence sin(c*x) indicates a periodic potential (e.g., pendulum gravity)
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or has autonomous damping
- Cubic position terms with sign opposite to linear term indicate a double-well (Duffing) potential
- Phase-space structure: if dv_dt depends only on x and v (not t), the system is autonomous and can be analyzed via phase portraits
